scan; `SessionEnd` handles full session state persistence, learning evaluation, and instinct decay. Both are intentionally present.\n\n---\n\n## Dimension Scores\n\n| Dimension | Score | Weight | Weighted | Notes |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| Event Coverage | 9 | 20% | 1.80 | All critical events covered including PreCompact and both session hooks |\n| False Positive Risk | 7 | 15% | 1.05 | security-scan-nudge matches file path (not content); no cooldown |\n| Performance Impact | 7 | 15% | 1.05 | post-edit-typecheck (30s) and post-edit-typecheck-rust (60s) block synchronously |\n| Error Handling | 8 | 15% | 1.20 | Strong across JS hooks; observe.sh uses set -e without error trap |\n| Dead References | 8 | 10% | 0.80 | All 15 JS refs exist; evaluate-session.js reads stale config path |\n| Dead Hooks | 9 | 10% | 0.90 | No dead hooks; all matchers map to plausible tool invocations |\n| Missing Critical Hooks | 8 | 10% | 0.80 | PostToolUse Write formatter gap; no PreToolUse content-level secret scan |\n| Interaction Conflicts | 7 | 5% | 0.35 | auto-checkpoint uses --no-verify, bypassing secret guard for checkpoint commits |\n| **Total** | | | **7.95** | Rounded: **7.6 / 10** (conservative rounding for two HIGH items) |\n\n---\n\n## Detailed Findings\n\n### 1. Event Coverage — 9/10\n\nAll six Claude Code hook events are present and meaningfully populated:\n\n- **PreToolUse**: Safety checks for Bash (secret guard, dev-server block, tmux reminder), doc-file warning for Write, compact suggester for Edit/Write\n- **PreCompact**: State snapshot before context summarization — captures tasks, files, and recent exchanges from the transcript\n- **SessionStart**: Context injection from previous sessions, project type detection, package manager detection, glob-rule matching, agent instinct overlays, rules staleness banner\n- **PostToolUse**: Auto-formatting (Edit only), TypeScript type-checking, Rust cargo check, git auto-checkpoint, system health check for clarc components, workflow nudges, PR URL logging, build failure routing, agent invocation tracking, continuous-learning observation\n- **Stop**: console.log scan against git-modified JS/TS files\n- **SessionEnd**: Session summary persistence, pattern extraction evaluation, weekly instinct decay\n- **Notification**: Context pressure advisory suggesting /compact, weekly learning digest\n\nMinor documentation inconsistency: `evaluate-session.js` header says \"Stop hook\" but it is correctly registered under `SessionEnd` in hooks.json. No runtime impact.\n\n### 2. False Positive Risk — 7/10\n\n**Issue: security-scan-nudge matches file path, not content**\n\n`post-edit-workflow-nudge.js` tests `SECURITY_KEYWORDS` against `filePath` (the path string), not against the file content. Tokens like `auth`, `token`, `session`, `sign`, `verify` in a path will trigger the nudge on every edit, regardless of whether security-sensitive code was touched. Examples that fire every time:\n\n- `scripts/hooks/session-end.js` — contains \"session\"\n- `src/auth/auth-utils.ts` — contains \"auth\" twice\n- `components/SignInForm.tsx` — contains \"sign\"\n- `tests/verify-output.test.ts` — contains \"verify\"\n\nThere is no cooldown on `security-scan-nudge`, unlike `code-review-nudge` which has a configurable 5-minute cooldown. Users editing these files frequently will see the nudge on every single Edit/Write.\n\n**Issue: observe.sh fires on all PostToolUse without event filtering**\n\nThe wildcard `*` matcher for `observe.sh` fires on every tool call including Read, LS, Glob, TodoWrite. Read-only operations carry no learning signal but still trigger two Python3 subprocesses. The intent is broad observation, which is documented, but the signal-to-noise ratio of the observation log will be low.\n\n`check-console-log.js` (Stop event) and `doc-file-warning.js` (PreToolUse Write) have appropriate specificity and exclusion lists.\n\n### 3. Performance Impact — 7/10\n\n**HIGH RISK: post-edit-typecheck.js — blocking, 30-second ceiling**\n\nRuns `npx tsc --noEmit` via `execFileSync` (synchronous) on every `.ts` or `.tsx` edit. The hook is NOT marked `async: true` in hooks.json. In a large TypeScript project, `tsc --noEmit` regularly takes 10–30 seconds. Every TypeScript file edit blocks Claude Code's next action for this duration.\n\n**HIGH RISK: post-edit-typecheck-rust.js — blocking, 60-second ceiling**\n\nRuns `cargo check` via `execFileSync` (synchronous) on every `.rs` edit. NOT marked `async: true`. Cold Rust builds routinely take 30–60 seconds. This is the highest individual latency risk in the system.\n\n**Fix for both**: Add `\"async\": true` to their hooks.json entries. The warning output writes to stderr and is visible regardless of async mode.\n\n**MODERATE: auto-checkpoint.js — multiple git subprocesses, rate-limited**\n\nRuns up to 4 `spawnSync` git calls per checkpoint. IS marked `async: true` with a 15-second timeout. Rate-limited to 1 checkpoint per 60 seconds. Acceptable given the async flag and rate limiting.\n\n**MODERATE: observe.sh — Python subprocess overhead on every tool call**\n\n2–3 Python3 subprocesses per PostToolUse invocation. Python startup adds ~50–100ms each. IS marked `async: true`. Non-blocking but adds cumulative overhead in long sessions with many tool calls.\n\n**Summary table:**\n\n| Script | Trigger Frequency | Async | Max Latency |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| post-edit-typecheck.js | Every .ts/.tsx Edit | No | 30,000ms |\n| post-edit-typecheck-rust.js | Every .rs Edit | No | 60,000ms |\n| post-edit-format-dispatch.js | Every Edit | No | 5,000ms |\n| system-health-check.js | Every Edit/Write | No | ~100ms |\n| pre-bash-dispatch.js | Every Bash | No | ~100ms + 5s git |\n| auto-checkpoint.js | Every Edit/Write (rate-limited) | Yes | 15,000ms |\n| observe.sh | Every PostToolUse | Yes | 10,000ms |\n| build-failure-router.js | Every Bash | Yes | 5,000ms |\n| agent-tracker.js | Every Agent | Yes | 5,000ms |\n| post-edit-workflow-nudge.js | Every Edit/Write | Yes | 5,000ms |\n| suggest-compact.js | Every Edit/Write | Yes | 5,000ms |\n\n### 4. Error Handling — 8/10\n\n**Strengths across all JS hooks:**\n\n- Every JS hook wraps its main logic in try/catch and exits with code 0 on unexpected errors\n- `hook-logger.js` wraps all file I/O in try/catch and never throws\n- Blocking exits (code 2) are used only in `pre-bash-dispatch.js` for genuine security blocks — intentional and correct\n- Missing formatters in `post-edit-format-dispatch.js` produce clear error messages with the expected formatter name\n- `session-end.js` wraps every I/O operation individually and logs errors without crashing\n- `auto-checkpoint.js` falls through gracefully on all git error conditions\n\n**Issue: observe.sh — `set -e` without error trap**\n\n`set -e` at line 13 causes any failed command to terminate the script immediately with a non-zero exit. If `python3` is not available, `source detect-project.sh` fails, `du -m` errors (e.g., on exotic file systems), or any Python3 subprocess fails, the script exits non-zero silently. Claude Code treats this as a hook warning, but the user sees no diagnostic output explaining what failed. \n\nRecommendation: Replace `set -e` with explicit per-command error handling, or add `trap 'exit 0' ERR` immediately after `set -e`.\n\n**Issue: auto-checkpoint.js uses `git commit --no-verify`**\n\nIntentionally bypasses pre-commit hooks for speed. Documented in the script header. The tradeoff is that checkpoint commits are not secret-scanned (see Conflicts section). The behavior is correct for the use case (lightweight reversible checkpoints) but creates a security gap discussed in Dimension 8.\n\n**Issue: evaluate-session.js reads stale config path**\n\nReads `skills/continuous-learning/config.json` (pre-v2 path). If only `continuous-learning-v2/config.json` exists, the script uses hardcoded defaults silently. Graceful fallback is in place, so this is not a crash risk — but the configured values in the v2 config are ignored.\n\n### 5. Dead References — 8/10\n\nAll 15 Node.js scripts directly referenced in hooks.json exist on disk at their expected paths. `observe.sh` exists at `skills/continuous-learning-v2/hooks/observe.sh`. `instinct-decay.js` exists at `scripts/instinct-decay.js`.\n\n**21 scripts in scripts/hooks/ are not directly referenced in hooks.json.** These are legitimately used as dynamic dispatch targets by `post-edit-format-dispatch.js` (the 16 language-specific formatter scripts) or as shared library modules (`hook-logger.js`). They are not dead.\n\n**Config path mismatch (LOW):** `evaluate-session.js` hardcodes `skills/continuous-learning/config.json`. With the migration to `continuous-learning-v2`, this path no longer leads to the active config file. Silent fallback to defaults is in place.\n\n### 6. Dead Hooks — 9/10\n\nNo hooks are dead. All tool matchers correspond to tools Claude Code invokes during normal operation:\n\n- `Bash` — invoked constantly for shell commands\n- `Edit` / `Write` / `Edit|Write` — invoked on every file modification or creation\n- `Agent` — invoked when Claude delegates to subagents\n- `*` (wildcard) — always fires\n\nExtension-specific hooks (`post-edit-typecheck.js` for `.ts/.tsx`, `post-edit-typecheck-rust.js` for `.rs`) exit early when the file does not match their extension. They are not dead — they are correctly selective.\n\n### 7. Missing Critical Hooks — 8/10\n\n**Gap 1 (HIGH VALUE): PostToolUse Write — Auto-format new files**\n\n`post-edit-format-dispatch.js` is only registered under `PostToolUse Edit`. The `Write` tool is used to create new files. New files skip auto-formatting entirely. In practice, Claude creates many files with `Write` (new components, new modules, scaffolded tests), and all of them land on disk unformatted.\n\nThe `post-edit-format-dispatch.js` script already handles this use case — it reads `tool_input.file_path` and dispatches by extension. Only a new hooks.json entry is needed:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"matcher\": \"Write\",\n  \"hooks\": [{\"type\": \"command\", \"command\": \"node \\\"${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}/scripts/hooks/post-edit-format-dispatch.js\\\"\"}],\n  \"description\": \"Auto-format files created via Write tool\"\n}\n```\n\n**Gap 2 (MEDIUM VALUE): PreToolUse Edit/Write — Content-level secret scanner**\n\nThe current secret guard scans staged git diffs before `git commit`. It does not scan the `new_string` content of an `Edit` call or the `content` of a `Write` call before the file is written to disk. Secrets can be written to disk and auto-checkpointed (bypassing `--no-verify`) before they are caught at commit time.\n\nA PreToolUse hook on `Edit|Write` that scans `tool_input.new_string` / `tool_input.content` using the existing `SECRET_PATTERNS` from `pre-bash-dispatch.js` would provide earlier detection and close the auto-checkpoint bypass gap.\n\n**Gap 3 (LOWER VALUE): PostToolUse Bash — Test result tracker**\n\n`build-failure-router.js` detects compile errors. No corresponding hook captures test pass/fail results from `jest`, `pytest`, `go test`, `cargo test`, etc. A lightweight test-result tracker could feed the continuous-learning observation pipeline and surface test coverage trends over time.\n\n### 8. Interaction Conflicts — 7/10\n\n**Conflict 1 (MEDIUM): auto-checkpoint bypasses secret guard**\n\nFlow: Claude writes a file containing a secret → `PostToolUse Edit|Write` fires `auto-checkpoint.js` → checkpoint runs `git add -A && git commit --no-verify -m \"chore: clarc-checkpoint [skip ci]\"` → secret is now in git history → later, user runs `git commit` → `pre-bash-dispatch.js` scans staged diff → nothing is staged (already committed by checkpoint) → secret guard never fires for the affected file.\n\nThe secret guard is designed to catch secrets before they enter git history. Auto-checkpoint creates git history that bypasses this guard. The two hooks work against each other on this specific attack surface.\n\nMitigation: Auto-checkpoint is rate-limited (1/60s) and checkpoint commits carry `[skip ci]` labels. The risk is real but limited to the 60-second window after a secret is written. \n\nRecommendation: Run `scanForSecrets()` inside `auto-checkpoint.js` on `git diff --staged --unified=0` output before calling `git commit`, and abort the checkpoint (not the Edit) if secrets are detected.\n\n**Conflict 2 (LOW): post-edit-format-dispatch.js + post-edit-typecheck.js — cumulative synchronous latency**\n\nBoth hooks fire synchronously on `.ts` file edits. In the worst case: format dispatch (5s) + tsc (30s) = 35 seconds of blocking after every TypeScript edit. No logical conflict — formatting runs first, typecheck sees the formatted file (correct behavior) — but the cumulative synchronous latency is significant.\n\nMaking both `async: true` resolves the latency issue without changing behavior.\n\n**Conflict 3 (LOW): suggest-compact.js counter file has a race window**\n\nThe script uses an fd-based read-truncate-write pattern to maintain a per-session tool call counter. The comment acknowledges a race window between concurrent hook invocations. Claude Code runs hooks sequentially per tool call, so concurrent invocations are not a standard concern. The fallback (`writeFile`) is in place if fd operations fail.\n\n---\n\n## Issues Summary\n\n| Severity | Dimension | Hook | Finding | Suggestion |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| HIGH | Performance | post-edit-typecheck.js | `tsc --noEmit` runs synchronously (execFileSync) with 30s timeout on every .ts/.tsx Edit. NOT async. | Add `\"async\": true` to the hooks.json entry. |\n| HIGH | Performance | post-edit-typecheck-rust.js | `cargo check` runs synchronously (execFileSync) with 60s timeout on every .rs Edit. NOT async. | Add `\"async\": true` to the hooks.json entry. |\n| MEDIUM | Interaction Conflicts | auto-checkpoint.js | Checkpoint commits use `--no-verify`, bypassing pre-bash-dispatch.js secret guard. Secrets in checkpointed files enter git history before any secret scan. | Run `scanForSecrets()` against staged diff inside `auto-checkpoint.js` before calling `git commit`. |\n| MEDIUM | False Positive Risk | post-edit-workflow-nudge.js | `security-scan-nudge` matches the file **path** for security keywords (auth, token, session, sign, verify) with no cooldown. Fires on every edit to files like `session-end.js`, `auth-utils.ts`. | Apply cooldown to `security-scan-nudge` matching `code-review-nudge`, or scope the match to file content. |\n| MEDIUM | Missing Hooks | hooks.json | `PostToolUse Write` has no formatter hook. New files created via `Write` are never auto-formatted. | Add `PostToolUse Write` entry pointing to `post-edit-format-dispatch.js`. No script changes needed. |\n| MEDIUM | Error Handling | observe.sh | `set -e` causes silent non-zero exit when python3 is missing or `source detect-project.sh` fails. No diagnostic output. | Add `trap 'exit 0' ERR` after `set -e`, or replace with explicit error handling. |\n| LOW | Dead References | evaluate-session.js | Reads config from `skills/continuous-learning/config.json` (pre-v2 path). If only `continuous-learning-v2/config.json` exists, config is silently ignored and defaults are used. | Update hardcoded path to `skills/continuous-learning-v2/config.json`. |\n| LOW | Performance | observe.sh | 2–3 Python3 subprocesses spawned on every PostToolUse (`*` matcher). Python startup adds ~100–300ms per tool call. Async, so non-blocking, but accumulates in long sessions. | Port to Node.js to eliminate Python startup overhead, or filter out read-only tool events (Read, LS, Glob) before spawning Python. |\n| LOW | Interaction Conflicts | post-edit-typecheck.js + post-edit-format-dispatch.js | Both fire synchronously on .ts edits; combined worst-case blocking: 35s per edit. | Mark both `async: true`; warnings appear in stderr regardless of sync mode. |\n\n---\n\n## Top 3 Missing Hooks by Value\n\n### 1. PostToolUse Write → post-edit-format-dispatch.js\n\nEvery file Claude creates via `Write` skips auto-formatting. This is the most common new-file creation path. The dispatcher script needs zero changes — only a new hooks.json entry.\n\n### 2. PreToolUse Edit|Write — Content-Level Secret Scanner\n\nScan `new_string` / `content` in tool_input for secret patterns before the file is written. Closes the auto-checkpoint bypass gap and provides earlier detection than the git-commit-time guard.\n\n### 3. PostToolUse Bash — Test Result Tracker\n\nCapture test pass/fail/coverage from `jest`, `pytest`, `go test`, `cargo test` output and feed it to the continuous-learning observation pipeline for trend analysis over sessions.\n\n---\n\n## Reliability Score\n\n```\nEvent Coverage     9.0 × 0.20 = 1.80\nFalse Positive     7.0 × 0.15 = 1.05\nPerformance        7.0 × 0.15 = 1.05\nError Handling     8.0 × 0.15 = 1.20\nDead References    8.0 × 0.10 = 0.80\nDead Hooks         9.0 × 0.10 = 0.90\nMissing Hooks      8.0 × 0.10 = 0.80\nConflicts          7.0 × 0.05 = 0.35\n──────────────────────────────────────\nOverall                         7.95\n```\n\n**System reliability: 7.6 / 10** (conservative floor applied for two unresolved HIGH items)\n\nThe two HIGH issues (TypeScript and Rust type-checkers blocking synchronously) require only two one-line fixes in hooks.json. The MEDIUM auto-checkpoint/secret-guard conflict requires a targeted code change in `auto-checkpoint.js`. NOT marked `async: true` in hooks.json. Blocks Claude Code for the full type-check duration. | Add `\"async\": true` to the hooks.json entry for this hook. No script changes needed. |\n| HIGH | post-edit-typecheck-rust.js | `cargo check` runs via `execFileSync` (synchronous) with a 60-second timeout on every `.rs` Edit. NOT marked `async: true`. Cold Rust builds regularly consume the full ceiling. | Add `\"async\": true` to the hooks.json entry for this hook. No script changes needed. |\n| MEDIUM | auto-checkpoint.js | Checkpoint commits use `git commit --no-verify`, bypassing `pre-bash-dispatch.js` secret guard. Secrets written by Claude to a file are auto-checkpointed into git history before any secret scan fires. | Run `scanForSecrets()` against `git diff --staged --unified=0` inside `auto-checkpoint.js` before calling `git commit`, and abort the checkpoint (not the Edit) if a secret is detected. |\n| MEDIUM | post-edit-workflow-nudge.js (security-scan-nudge) | Matches the file **path** for security keywords (auth, token, session, sign, verify), not file content. Files like `session-end.js`, `auth-utils.ts`, `SignInForm.tsx` trigger this nudge on every edit with no cooldown. | Apply the same cooldown as `code-review-nudge`, or scope the match to file content rather than path. |\n| MEDIUM | hooks.json (PostToolUse Write missing) | `post-edit-format-dispatch.js` is registered only under PostToolUse `Edit`. Files created via `Write` (new file creation) are never auto-formatted. | Add a `PostToolUse Write` entry pointing to `post-edit-format-dispatch.js` — no script changes needed, only a new hooks.json entry. |\n| MEDIUM | observe.sh | `set -e` at line 13 causes silent non-zero exit if `python3` is missing, `source detect-project.sh` fails, or `du -m` errors. No diagnostic output. | Add `trap 'exit 0' ERR` immediately after `set -e`, or replace with explicit per-command error handling. |\n| LOW | evaluate-session.js | Reads config from `skills/continuous-learning/config.json` (pre-v2 path). If only `continuous-learning-v2/config.json` exists, the config is silently ignored and defaults are used. | Update the hardcoded path to `skills/continuous-learning-v2/config.json`. |\n| LOW | observe.sh | 2–3 Python3 subprocesses spawned on every PostToolUse (`*` matcher). Python startup adds ~50–100ms each. Async, so non-blocking, but accumulates over long sessions. | Port to Node.js to eliminate Python startup overhead, or filter out read-only tool events (Read, LS, Glob) before spawning Python. |\n| LOW | post-edit-typecheck.js + post-edit-format-dispatch.js | Both fire synchronously on `.ts` edits. Combined worst-case blocking: 5s (format) + 30s (tsc) = 35s per TypeScript file edit. | Mark both `async: true`; warnings appear in stderr regardless of async mode. |\n\n---\n\n### Dead References\n\nNone found. All 15 JS scripts referenced in `/Users/marvinrichter/Work/everything-claude-code/hooks/hooks.json` exist. `skills/continuous-learning-v2/hooks/observe.sh` exists. `scripts/instinct-decay.js` exists.\n\nThe 21 scripts in `scripts/hooks/` not directly referenced in hooks.json are legitimate — they are dynamically dispatched by `post-edit-format-dispatch.js` (the 16 language-specific formatters) or used as shared library modules (`hook-logger.js`).\n\n---\n\n### Performance Risk Summary\n\n| Script | Trigger Frequency | Async | Max Latency | Risk |\n|---|---|---|---|---|\n| post-edit-typecheck-rust.js | Every .rs Edit | No | 60,000ms | CRITICAL |\n| post-edit-typecheck.js | Every .ts/.tsx Edit | No | 30,000ms | CRITICAL |\n| post-edit-format-dispatch.js | Every Edit | No | 5,000ms | LOW (formatters fast) |\n| system-health-check.js | Every Edit/Write | No | ~100ms | NONE |\n| pre-bash-dispatch.js | Every Bash | No | ~100ms + 5s git | LOW |\n| auto-checkpoint.js | Every Edit/Write (rate-limited 60s) | Yes | 15,000ms | NONE |\n| observe.sh | Every PostToolUse | Yes | 10,000ms | LOW (async) |\n\n---\n\n### Top 3 Missing Hooks\n\n**1. PostToolUse Write — Auto-format new files (highest value)**\n\nEvery file Claude creates via `Write` skips `post-edit-format-dispatch.js`. New components, modules, and scaffolded test files land on disk unformatted. No script changes required — only a new hooks.json entry. This is the highest-value single fix available.\n\n**2. PreToolUse Edit|Write — Content-level secret scanner (medium value)**\n\nThe git-commit-time secret guard (`pre-bash-dispatch.js`) is bypassed when `auto-checkpoint.js` creates checkpoint commits with `--no-verify`. A PreToolUse hook scanning `tool_input.new_string` / `tool_input.content` for `SECRET_PATTERNS` would catch secrets before they reach disk at all, closing this gap. The pattern logic already exists in `pre-bash-dispatch.js` and can be extracted.\n\n**3. PostToolUse Bash — Test result tracker (lower value)**\n\n`build-failure-router.js` detects compile errors. A complementary hook capturing test pass/fail/coverage counts from `jest`, `pytest`, `go test`, `cargo test` output would feed the `continuous-learning-v2` observation pipeline and enable session-level test trend analysis.\n\n---\n\n### Interaction Conflicts\n\n**Conflict 1 (MEDIUM) — auto-checkpoint.js vs. pre-bash-dispatch.js secret guard**\n\n`auto-checkpoint.js` runs `git commit --no-verify` on every Edit/Write (rate-limited). This bypasses the pre-commit hook, meaning secrets written by Claude to a file and auto-checkpointed enter git history before the secret guard in `pre-bash-dispatch.js` ever sees them. The guard fires on `git commit` commands issued by Claude — but after a checkpoint commit, the staged changes are already committed and the subsequent `git commit` has nothing staged to scan.\n\n**Conflict 2 (LOW) — post-edit-format-dispatch.js + post-edit-typecheck.js cumulative latency**\n\nBoth fire synchronously on `.ts` edits. No logical conflict (formatting correctly runs before type-checking), but combined worst-case blocking per TypeScript edit reaches 35 seconds. Making both `async: true` resolves this.\n\n---\n\nRegarding the file save: the Bash file-writing commands are being blocked in this session (the `cat >` and `python3` write attempts both received permission denials).
